## lattice-system

A Lean 4 + Mathlib formalization project targeting general lattice models.
This project subsumes and generalizes the earlier
[ising-model](https://github.com/phasetr/ising-model) project, progressively
covering classical spin systems, quantum spin systems, Hubbard, BCS,
CAR algebras, and eventually lattice QCD.

## Design axis: graphs, not lattices

Despite the name, the **primary combinatorial abstraction in this
library is a graph `(Έ¦, E_Έ¦)`** βÄî finite for finite-volume work and
infinite for the thermodynamic-limit / algebraic-formulation work
that is a major long-term goal βÄî not "a lattice". Concrete lattices
(the 1D chain, square / cubic grids, infinite chains, β³Λ^d, βÄΠ) appear
only as specific instances such as `SimpleGraph.pathGraph`,
`SimpleGraph.cycleGraph`, products of these, or their infinite
analogues. This convention follows the standard mathematical-physics
literature on many-body systems on graphs (Lieb's theorem on
bipartite lattices, the MarshallβÄ™LiebβÄ™Mattis theorem, Miyao 2021
¬ß3, βÄΠ) and aligns the project with mathlib's `SimpleGraph`
foundations.

Finite-volume work uses `Έ¦ : Type*` together with `[Fintype Έ¦]`
when needed (e.g. for traces, partition functions, finite sums of
local terms); infinite-volume work drops the `Fintype` assumption
and uses graphs over types like `β³Λ` or `β³Λ^d` instead.

The bridge from a `SimpleGraph` to the pairwise coupling
`J : Έ¦ βÜ£ Έ¦ βÜ£ β³²` consumed by `heisenbergHamiltonian` (and similar
operators) lives in `LatticeSystem.Lattice.Graph` (`couplingOf`).
Existing chain coupling families (`openChainCoupling`,
`periodicChainCoupling`) are characterised as
`couplingOf (pathGraph _) _` and `couplingOf (cycleGraph _) _`
respectively.

## Scope

| Area | Stage | Typical references |
|---|---|---|
| Classical spin systems | Inherited from ising-model | Friedli-Velenik, Glimm-Jaffe |
| Quantum spin systems | Current focus | Tasaki, Nielsen-Chuang (cross-check) |
| Hubbard / BCS | Medium term | Tasaki 1998, Bru-Pedra |
| CAR-algebraic formulation | Medium-long term | Araki-Moriya, Bru-Pedra |
| Thermodynamic limit (infinite graphs) | Long term, **major project goal** | Simon, Friedli-Velenik, Bratteli-Robinson |
| Lattice QCD | Longest term | Aarts, Davies |

## Refactoring conventions and review criteria

A **single-source-of-truth document** for refactoring conventions
applied as the review checklist on every pull request:
[Refactoring conventions and review criteria](refactoring-conventions.html).
Topics: test methods (decide / bridge / small-exhaustive / shim /
`#guard_msgs`), module-split criteria, generic / dedup conventions,
deprecation window policy, naming / docstring rules, linter
exceptions, public-doc synchronisation.

The companion page [Deprecation window](deprecations.html) tracks
currently-deprecated public declarations, the `since` date,
recommended replacement, and earliest-removal window.

| P1i (Tasaki ¬ß2.4) | Heisenberg Hamiltonian on the fully-polarised state: `H |sβÄΠsβü© = (βàë_{x,y} J(x,y)¬Ζ(if x=y then 3/4 else 1/4)) ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©` (eq. (2.4.5), `S = 1/2`); plus the ladder step `≈€_tot^¬± ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©` preserves the same H-eigenvalue (eqs. (2.4.7)/(2.4.9), `S = 1/2`) and its iterated form `(≈€_tot^¬±)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©` for every `k : β³ï`; plus `[H, Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ] = 0` for the global rotation (eq. (2.4.7) operator-level), the single-axis rotated constant-spin state `Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©` shares the H-eigenvalue, and the two-axis spin-coherent state `Ο¦^(3)_œï Ο¦^(2)_ΈΗ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü© = |Έû_ΈΗ,œïβü©` (eq. (2.4.6) for `s = 0`); plus the magnetic-quantum-number labelling `≈€tot^(3) ¬Ζ (≈€tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |βÜë..βÜëβü© = (Smax - k) ¬Ζ (≈€tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |βÜë..βÜëβü©` (eq. (2.4.9), unnormalised, lowering from highest weight) and its dual `≈€tot^(3) ¬Ζ (≈€tot^+)^k ¬Ζ |βÜ™..βÜ™βü© = (-Smax + k) ¬Ζ (≈€tot^+)^k ¬Ζ |βÜ™..βÜ™βü©` (eq. (2.4.9), unnormalised, raising from lowest weight); plus the Casimir invariance `≈€tot¬≤ ¬Ζ (≈€tot^βà™)^k ¬Ζ |s..sβü© = Smax(Smax+1) ¬Ζ (≈€tot^βà™)^k ¬Ζ |s..sβü©` for any constant `s`. For the matched highest/lowest-weight ladders, the unnormalised iterates `(≈€tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |βÜë..βÜëβü©` and `(≈€tot^+)^k ¬Ζ |βÜ™..βÜ™βü©` carry `(H, ≈€tot¬≤, ≈€tot^(3))` simultaneous eigenvalues `(c_J, Smax(Smax+1), Smaxβà™k)`; plus the boundary annihilations `≈€tot^- ¬Ζ |βÜ™..βÜ™βü© = 0` and `≈€tot^+ ¬Ζ |βÜë..βÜëβü© = 0` ensuring the ladder terminates after spanning all `2Smax + 1 = |Έ¦| + 1` magnetisation sectors βÄî building toward the full |ΈΠ_Mβü© / |Έû_ΈΗ,œïβü© ferromagnetic ground-state space | Done |
| P1g | Gibbs state `œ¹ = e^{-Έ≤H}/Z`, `Tr(œ¹) = 1`, `βü®1βü© = 1`, `Z(0) = dim`, `Z(0) βâ† 0`, linearity `βü®Oβ²¹+Oβ²²βü© = βü®Oβ²¹βü©+βü®Oβ²²βü©`, `βü®c¬ΖOβü© = c¬Ζβü®Oβü©`, `βü®-Oβü© = -βü®Oβü©`, `βü®Aβà£Bβü© = βü®Aβü©βà£βü®Bβü©`, `βü®ΈΘ fβü© = ΈΘ βü®fβü©`, `[œ¹, H] = 0`, reality of `βü®Oβü©` for Hermitian `O`, conservation `βü®[H,A]βü© = 0`, anticommutator real / commutator imaginary, `(βü®H¬ΖOβü©).im = 0`, Έ≤ = 0 closed form `œ¹_0 = I/dim` and `βü®Aβü©_0 = Tr A / dim`, one-parameter group property `e^{-(Έ≤β²¹+Έ≤β²²)H} = e^{-Έ≤β²¹H} ¬Ζ e^{-Έ≤β²²H}` and invertibility, exact discrete semigroup identity `e^{-(nΈ≤)H} = (e^{-Έ≤H})^n` (extended to `n : β³Λ` via `gibbsExp_inv`) | Done |

(2.3.6)), action on `|œà^βÜëβü©` / `|œà^βÜ™βü©`, additivity, antilinearity, single-spin **Kramers degeneracy** `Έ‰Χ²¬≤ = -1Χ²` (Tasaki eq. ΈΠ_NΟ©elβü© = -(1/4)` (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 (2.5.4) ingredient), per-bond `≈€^z ¬Ζ ≈€^z` correlation `-(1/4)` and off-diagonal correlator vanishing, parallel-bond expectation `+1/4`, K=1 chain Heisenberg energy `J/2`, time-reversal `Έ‰Χ²_tot ¬Ζ |ΈΠ_NΟ©elβü©` action across all dimensions, Marshall sign machinery (generic `marshallSignOf` + chain / 2D / 3D specialisations + `flipConfig` + Marshall Ο½ time-reversal bridge), the **generic graph-centric `neelStateOf : (V βÜ£ Bool) βÜ£ ((V βÜ£ Fin 2) βÜ£ β³²)`** primitive (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 (2.5.2) graph-centric form) of which the chain / 2D / 3D versions are 1-line corollaries via the `_eq_neelConfigOf` / `_eq_neelStateOf` bridges, the **Marshall-dressed standard basis** `marshallDressedBasis A œÉ := marshallSignOf A œÉ βÄΔ basisVec œÉ` (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 (2.5.8)) with orthonormality and `H_M`-membership, the **realness of dressed Heisenberg matrix elements** for real coupling `J` (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 p. 41, Property (i): each `((spinHalfDot x y) œÉ œÉ').im = 0`, hence `((heisenbergHamiltonian J) œÉ œÉ').im = 0`, hence the dressed bilinear pairing has zero imaginary part), the **Marshall sign trick** (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 p. 41, Property (ii)): for real non-negative `J` supported on bipartite bonds and `œÉ βâ† œÉ'`, the dressed off-diagonal Heisenberg pairing has non-positive real part, the **swap-connectivity** (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 p. 41βÄ™42, Property (iii)): for a connected graph `G` and any `œÉ x βâ† œÉ y`, the configurations `œÉ` and `basisSwap œÉ x y` are connected by a chain of single-edge swaps, and the **MarshallβÄ™LiebβÄ™Mattis Theorem 2.2 in `H_0` (matrix level)**: assembled across PRs Έ±-5a through Έ±-5o, the shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `B = c ¬Ζ I βà£ M` (symmetric, non-negative, irreducible on `H_0`) admits a unique-up-to-positive-scalar strictly positive PerronβÄ™Frobenius eigenvector βÄî equivalent to the matrix-level Tasaki (2.5.4) ground-state expansion `ΈΘ_œÉ c_œÉ \|Έ®ΧÉ^œÉβü©` with `c_œÉ > 0` βÄî first five steps of the MarshallβÄ™LiebβÄ™Mattis Theorem 2.2 formalization track (Issue #412) | In progress |

| P1m (Tasaki ¬ß2.5, generic-S sector form) | **Spin-S MarshallβÄ™LiebβÄ™Mattis Theorem 2.2 on the magnetization sector**: generalisation of P1k from spin-1/2 / `H_0` to general spin `S` (`N = 2S`) and arbitrary magnetization sector `M` via the subtype `magConfigS V N M`. Bipartite raise/lower reachability (Έ≥-3 connectivity for general spin) lifted to the sector subtype. Marshall sign conjugation forward (#853) + inverse (#854) gives a real-form sector eigenvector existence with Marshall sign structure. Eigenvector uniqueness (#854) at fixed `ΈΦ` and eigenvalue uniqueness (#856, via dressed-sector symmetry + Rayleigh identity). Bundled real-form ground-state theorems: same-`ΈΦ` form (#855) and forced-eigenvalue form (#859). Complex-form bridge: complex sector matrix Hermiticity + real-βÜî-complex eigenvector correspondence (#857, #858, #861). Generic spin `S`, arbitrary bipartite-antiferromagnetic Heisenberg coupling supported on a connected bipartite graph, with the intermediate-existence hypothesis. The next step is the lift from the magnetization sector to the FULL Hilbert space βÄî comparing ground-state energies across magnetization sectors. | Done |

(10.1.5))**; **SU(2) algebra: `[≈€^z, ≈€^-] = -≈€^-`, eigenvalue preservation and decrement by `≈€^-` (Tasaki ¬ß9.3.3, ¬ß11.1.1)**) |

| P4 | Thermodynamic limit, phase transitions | Not started |

## Formalized theorems

All items below are formally proved with **zero `sorry`**. Full
mathematical statements and proof sketches are in
[`tex/proof-guide.tex`](https://github.com/phasetr/lattice-system/blob/main/tex/proof-guide.tex).

### Single-site Pauli operators

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß2.1 eq. (2.1.8), p. 15. Cross-checked with Nielsen-Chuang
¬ß2.1.3 Figure 2.2 (pp. 65-66, definitions), Ex. 2.19 (p. 70,
Hermiticity), Ex. 2.41 (p. 78, `(œÉ^Έ±)¬≤ = I` and anticommutation),
Ex. 2.40 (p. 77, commutator, whence the cyclic products).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `pauliX/Y/Z_isHermitian` | `(œÉ^Έ±)βÄ† = œÉ^Έ±` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX/Y/Z_mul_self` | `(œÉ^Έ±)¬≤ = I` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_mul_pauliY` etc. | `œÉ^x œÉ^y = i¬ΖœÉ^z` (cyclic) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_anticomm_pauliY` etc. | `œÉ^Έ± œÉ^Έ≤ + œÉ^Έ≤ œÉ^Έ± = 0` (Έ± βâ† Έ≤) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |

### Spin-1/2 operators (Tasaki ¬ß2.1)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß2.1 eqs. (2.1.1), (2.1.7), (2.1.8), pp. 13-15.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfOp1/2/3` | `≈€^(Έ±) := œÉ^(Έ±) / 2` (Tasaki (2.1.7)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `pauliX_eq_two_smul_spinHalfOp1` etc. | `œÉ^(Έ±) = 2 ¬Ζ ≈€^(Έ±)` (Tasaki (2.1.8)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_isHermitian` etc. | `≈€^(Έ±)` is Hermitian | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_mul_self` etc. | `(≈€^(Έ±))¬≤ = (1/4) ¬Ζ I` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_anticomm_spinHalfOp2` etc. | anticommutation at `Έ± βâ† Έ≤` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_commutator_spinHalfOp2` etc. | `[≈€^(Έ±), ≈€^(Έ≤)] = i ¬Ζ ≈€^(Έ≥)` (Tasaki (2.1.1)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalf_total_spin_squared` | `ΈΘ (≈€^(Έ±))¬≤ = (3/4) ¬Ζ I`, i.e. `S(S+1)` with `S=1/2` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |

### Spin-1/2 rotation operators (Tasaki ¬ß2.1 eq. (2.1.26))

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß2.1 eq. (2.1.26), p. 17 (closed form) and eq. (2.1.23),
p. 16 (`Ο¦_{2œÄ} = -1` for half-odd-integer spin).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfRot1/2/3` | `Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ := cos(ΈΗ/2) ¬Ζ 1 - 2i ¬Ζ sin(ΈΗ/2) ¬Ζ ≈€^(Έ±)` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `spinHalfRot1/2/3_zero` | `Ο¦^(Έ±)_0 = 1` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `spinHalfRot1/2/3_adjoint` | `(Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ)βÄ† = Ο¦^(Έ±)_{-ΈΗ}` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

### 3D rotation matrices `R^(Έ±)_ΈΗ` (general ΈΗ, Tasaki ¬ß2.1 eq. (2.1.11))

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|

### Zβ²² Ο½ Zβ²² representation (Tasaki ¬ß2.1 eqs. (2.1.27)-(2.1.34))

The Zβ²² Ο½ Zβ²² structure is proved across files:
- S = 1/2 (projective, eq. (2.1.31)): `spinHalfRot*_pi_sq = -1`, anticommutation, products.
- S = 1 (genuine, eq. (2.1.27)): `spinOnePiRot*_sq = 1`, commutation.

See `Quantum/Z2Z2.lean` for the unified documentation.

### Spin-`S` operators (general S βâΞ 0, parameterised by `N = 2S : β³ï`)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body Systems*, ¬ß2.1 Problem 2.1.a (p. 15) and solution S.1 (p. 493).

Generic spin-`S` operators live on `Matrix (Fin (N + 1)) (Fin (N + 1)) β³²`, with `N = 2S : β³ï` (so `N = 1` β΅î `S = 1/2`, `N = 2` β΅î `S = 1`). Tracking issue #458 (Tasaki ¬ß2.1 P1d''' general-S generalisation).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinSOp3` | `≈€^(3) := diag(N/2, N/2 - 1, βÄΠ, -N/2)` for `N : β³ï` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus` / `spinSOpMinus` | raising/lowering operators with matrix entries `βàö(k¬Ζ(N βà£ k + 1))` (resp. `βàö((N βà£ k)(k + 1))`) on the immediate sub/super-diagonal | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp1` / `spinSOp2` | `≈€^(1) := (≈€^+ + ≈€^-) / 2`, `≈€^(2) := (≈€^+ βà£ ≈€^-) / (2 i)` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_apply_top` / `_bottom` | `≈€^+` annihilates `\|Nβü©` (highest weight); `≈€^-` annihilates `\|0βü©` (lowest weight) βÄî the ladder boundaries | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_commutator_spinSOp{Plus,Minus}` | **Cartan relations** `[≈€^{(3)}, ≈€^+] = ≈€^+` and `[≈€^{(3)}, ≈€^-] = -≈€^-`: `≈€^¬±` shift the magnetic quantum number by `¬±1`. Proved entry-wise via `Matrix.diagonal_mul` / `mul_diagonal` (Έ≤-2 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Algebra.lean` |
| `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_conjTranspose` / `spinSOp{1,2,3}_isHermitian` | adjointness `(≈€^+)α¥¥ = ≈€^-`, `(≈€^-)α¥¥ = ≈€^+`, and Hermiticity of `≈€^{(Έ±)}` for `Έ± βàà {1, 2, 3}` (Έ≤-3 of Issue #458). The ladder adjointness follows from the matrix-entry symmetry; `≈€^{(1)}` and `≈€^{(2)}` use the `1/2` and `1/(2i)` self-conjugacy facts | `Quantum/SpinS/Hermitian.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj` / `spinSOp3_sub_smul_mul_diagProj` / `_self_mul_diagProj` | the **diagonal projector** `P_k := diag(Έ¥_{i,k})` and the eigenvalue-action lemma `(≈€^{(3)} βà£ ΈΜ_j βÄΔ 1) ¬Ζ P_k = (ΈΜ_k βà£ ΈΜ_j) ¬Ζ P_k`, with the annihilation specialisation at `j = k` (Έ≤-4 of Issue #458). Foundation for the Lagrange-interpolation polynomial decomposition: each `P_k` will be expressed as `βàè_{j βâ† k} (≈€^{(3)} βà£ ΈΜ_j βÄΔ 1) / (ΈΜ_k βà£ ΈΜ_j)` in a follow-up PR | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProj.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_mul_diagProj` / `diagProj_mul_spinSOp3` / `spinSOp3_commute_diagProj` | the **eigenvalue equation** `≈€^{(3)} ¬Ζ P_k = ΈΜ_k ¬Ζ P_k` (where `ΈΜ_k = (N : β³²)/2 βà£ k`), with the symmetric `P_k ¬Ζ ≈€^{(3)} = ΈΜ_k ¬Ζ P_k` and the resulting commutativity. Both are diagonal-times-diagonal computations (Έ≤-5 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Lagrange.lean` |
| `mul_diagProj_apply` / `diagProj_mul_apply` / `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_mul_diagProj_apply` | **Column/row selection** by the diagonal projector: `(A ¬Ζ P_k)[i, j] = A[i, k]` if `j = k` else `0` (and dually for `P_k ¬Ζ A`). Specialised to `≈€^¬±` produces off-diagonal matrix units (Έ≤-6 of Issue #458) βÄî the building blocks of the polynomial decomposition theorem | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderProj.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_succ_mul_spinSOpMinus` | **Ladder recursion**: `≈€^+ ¬Ζ P_{k+1} ¬Ζ ≈€^- = (k + 1)(N βà£ k) ¬Ζ P_k`. The triple product collapses to a non-zero scalar multiple of `P_k`. Iterating from the lowest-weight projector `P_N` (itself a polynomial in `≈€^{(3)}`) yields every diagonal projector as a polynomial in `{1Χ², ≈€^{(Έ±)}}` (Έ≤-7 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderRecursion.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_first` / `spinSOpMinus_mul_diagProj_last` | **Ladder boundaries**: `≈€^+ ¬Ζ P_0 = 0` (top of ladder) and `≈€^- ¬Ζ P_N = 0` (bottom). The first/last columns of `≈€^¬±` vanish, so multiplication by `P_{0/N}` (which selects that column) gives `0`. Terminate the recursion at the highest- and lowest-weight projectors (Έ≤-8 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderBoundary.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_isHermitian` / `sum_spinSDiagProj_eq_one` | **Hermiticity** of each `P_k`, and the **resolution of the identity** `ΈΘ_k P_k = 1`. The latter is the cornerstone for the matrix-unit decomposition: combined with the off-diagonal matrix units (Έ≤-6, Έ≤-7), gives every matrix in `M_{N+1}(β³²)` (Έ≤-9 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjProperties.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_succ_eq_single` / `spinSOpMinus_mul_diagProj_eq_single` | **Off-diagonal matrix-unit decomposition**: `≈€^+ ¬Ζ P_{i+1} = βàö((i+1)(Nβà£i)) ¬Ζ E_{i, i+1}` and `≈€^- ¬Ζ P_i = βàö((Nβà£i)(i+1)) ¬Ζ E_{i+1, i}`, where `E_{a, b} := Matrix.single a b 1` is the (a, b) matrix unit (Έ≤-10 of Issue #458). These are the simplest off-diagonal matrix units expressible via `≈€^¬±` ladder action on diagonal projectors | `Quantum/SpinS/OffDiagUnit.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_sq_eq_diagonal` | `(≈€^{(3)})¬≤ = diag((N/2 βà£ i)¬≤)`. Step toward the **Casimir identity** `(≈€^{(1)})¬≤ + (≈€^{(2)})¬≤ + (≈€^{(3)})¬≤ = (N(N+2)/4) ¬Ζ 1` for general spin (Έ≤-11 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Op3Square.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_spinSOpMinus_eq_diagonal` | `≈€^+ ¬Ζ ≈€^- = diag((i + 1)(N βà£ i))`. The product is diagonal because `≈€^+[i, l] ¬Ζ ≈€^-[l, j]` is non-zero only when `l = i + 1 = j + 1`, forcing `i = j`. Combined with the analogous `≈€^- ¬Ζ ≈€^+` and `(≈€^{(3)})¬≤`, this assembles the Casimir identity (Έ≤-12 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PlusMinusDiag.lean` |
| `spinSOpMinus_mul_spinSOpPlus_eq_diagonal` | `≈€^- ¬Ζ ≈€^+ = diag(i ¬Ζ (N βà£ i + 1))`. Symmetric to Έ≤-12 with `≈€^¬±` swapped (Έ≤-13 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/MinusPlusDiag.lean` |
| `spinSOp1_sq_add_spinSOp2_sq` / `spinSOp_total_squared` | **Casimir identity** for general spin-`S`: `(≈€^{(1)})¬≤ + (≈€^{(2)})¬≤ + (≈€^{(3)})¬≤ = (N(N+2)/4) ¬Ζ 1`, equivalent to `S(S+1) ¬Ζ 1` for `S = N/2`. Proves the irreducible spin-`S` representation has Casimir eigenvalue `S(S+1)` (Schur's lemma). The intermediate identity `(≈€^{(1)})¬≤ + (≈€^{(2)})¬≤ = (1/2)(≈€^+ ¬Ζ ≈€^- + ≈€^- ¬Ζ ≈€^+)` is proved using `module` (Έ≤-14 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Casimir.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_mulVec_basis` | spin-`S` eigenstate equation `≈€^{(3)} ¬Ζ \|kβü© = (N/2 βà£ k) ¬Ζ \|kβü©`, where `\|kβü© := Pi.single k 1` is the `k`-th unit basis vector of `(Fin (N + 1) βÜ£ β³²)` (Έ≤-15 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Eigenstates.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mulVec_basis` / `spinSOpMinus_mulVec_basis` | **Ladder action on basis vectors**: `≈€^+ ¬Ζ \|kβü© = βàö(k(N βà£ k + 1)) ¬Ζ \|k βà£ 1βü©` for `k βâΞ 1`, and `≈€^- ¬Ζ \|kβü© = βàö((N βà£ k)(k + 1)) ¬Ζ \|k + 1βü©` for `k βâΛ N βà£ 1`. The standard SU(2) ladder relations on the magnetic-quantum-number basis (Έ≤-16 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderStates.lean` |
| `spinSOp_total_squared_mulVec_basis` | **Casimir eigenvalue on basis**: `(≈€)¬≤ ¬Ζ \|kβü© = (N(N+2)/4) ¬Ζ \|kβü©`. Direct consequence of `(≈€)¬≤ = (N(N+2)/4) ¬Ζ 1` (Έ≤-14) βÄî every basis vector has the universal Casimir eigenvalue, reflecting that the spin-`S` representation is a single irreducible (Schur) (Έ≤-17 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CasimirEigenvalue.lean` |
| `spinSOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}_commute_total_squared` | **Casimir invariance**: each `≈€^{(Έ±)}` and `≈€^¬±` commutes with the Casimir `(≈€)¬≤ = (N(N+2)/4) ¬Ζ 1`. Direct consequence of the scalar nature of the Casimir (Έ≤-18 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CasimirInvariance.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_commutator_spinSOpMinus` | **Third Cartan relation**: `[≈€^+, ≈€^-] = 2 ¬Ζ ≈€^{(3)}`. Combines Έ≤-12 (`≈€^+ ¬Ζ ≈€^- = diag((i + 1)(N βà£ i))`) and Έ≤-13 (`≈€^- ¬Ζ ≈€^+ = diag(i (N βà£ i + 1))`); the difference `(i+1)(N-i) βà£ i(N-i+1) = N βà£ 2i = 2(N/2 βà£ i)` matches `2 ¬Ζ ≈€^{(3)}` (Έ≤-19 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Cartan3.lean` |
| `spinSOp1_commutator_spinSOp2` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[≈€^{(1)}, ≈€^{(2)}] = i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(3)}`. Derived from the Cartan relations by algebraic manipulation through `≈€^{(1)} = (≈€^+ + ≈€^-)/2` and `≈€^{(2)} = (≈€^+ βà£ ≈€^-)/(2i)`: `(P+Q)(P-Q) βà£ (P-Q)(P+Q) = -2[P, Q] = -4 ≈€^{(3)}`, then scalar simplification `-1/I = I` (Έ≤-20 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator.lean` |
| `spinSOp2_commutator_spinSOp3` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[≈€^{(2)}, ≈€^{(3)}] = i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(1)}`. Derived from Cartan Έ≤-2 (`[≈€^{(3)}, ≈€^¬±] = ¬±≈€^¬±`) via `≈€^{(2)} = (≈€^+ βà£ ≈€^-)/(2i)`: the commutator reduces to `(1/(2i)) (-≈€^+ βà£ ≈€^-) = (-1/(2i)) ¬Ζ 2 ≈€^{(1)} = i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(1)}` (Έ≤-21 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator23.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_commutator_spinSOp1` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[≈€^{(3)}, ≈€^{(1)}] = i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(2)}`. Derived from Cartan Έ≤-2 via `≈€^{(1)} = (≈€^+ + ≈€^-)/2`: the commutator reduces to `(1/2) (≈€^+ βà£ ≈€^-) = (1/2) ¬Ζ (2i) ¬Ζ ≈€^{(2)} = i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(2)}`. Together with Έ≤-20 and Έ≤-21 this completes the standard SU(2) commutator algebra (Tasaki eq. (2.1.1)) for spin-`S` operators (Έ≤-22 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator31.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mul_self` / `spinSDiagProj_mul_of_ne` | **Idempotence and orthogonality** of the diagonal projectors `P_k = |kβü©βü®k|`: `P_k ¬Ζ P_k = P_k` and `P_i ¬Ζ P_j = 0` for `i βâ† j`. Combined with Έ≤-9 (`βàë_k P_k = 1`) this gives the spectral decomposition of the identity for `≈€^{(3)}` (Έ≤-23 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjOrtho.lean` |
| `aeval_diagonal` | **Polynomial evaluation at a diagonal matrix**: `aeval (Matrix.diagonal v) p = Matrix.diagonal (fun i => p.eval (v i))`. Foundational lemma for the Lagrange-interpolation step (Έ≤-25+) βÄî lets us pull a polynomial in `≈€^{(3)}` (a diagonal matrix) through to its scalar action on each diagonal entry. Proof by `Polynomial.induction_on'` on monomials and addition (Έ≤-24 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AevalDiagonal.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_eq_lagrange_aeval` | **Lagrange-interpolation formula for `P_k`**: `P_k = aeval (≈€^{(3)}) (Lagrange.basis Finset.univ (spinSOp3Eigen N) k)`, equivalently `P_k = βàè_{j βâ† k} (≈€^{(3)} βà£ ΈΜ_j βÄΔ 1)/(ΈΜ_k βà£ ΈΜ_j)` with `ΈΜ_j = (N : β³²)/2 βà£ j.val`. Combines Έ≤-24 (`aeval` of diagonal) with mathlib's `Lagrange.eval_basis_self` / `eval_basis_of_ne`. Each diagonal projector is therefore a **polynomial in `≈€^{(3)}`**, which combined with Έ≤-9 (`βàë P_k = 1`) gives an explicit polynomial decomposition of `1Χ²` (Έ≤-25 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LagrangeFormula.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_eq_one_add_I_smul_two` / `spinSOpMinus_eq_one_sub_I_smul_two` | **Inversion of the Cartesian definition**: `≈€^+ = ≈€^{(1)} + i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(2)}` and `≈€^- = ≈€^{(1)} βà£ i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(2)}`. The defining identities `≈€^{(1)} = (1/2)(≈€^+ + ≈€^-)`, `≈€^{(2)} = (1/(2i))(≈€^+ βà£ ≈€^-)` invert to express the ladder operators as **linear combinations** of the Hermitian Cartesian spin operators (Έ≤-26 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMAsOneTwo.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin_spinSOp3` / `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin` | **Diagonal projectors live in the algebra generated by the spin operators**: `P_k βàà Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(3)}}` (and a fortiori `P_k βàà Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(1)}, ≈€^{(2)}, ≈€^{(3)}}`). Promotes the Lagrange-interpolation formula (Έ≤-25) from "polynomial-evaluation" form to "subalgebra-membership" form via `Algebra.adjoin_singleton_eq_range_aeval` (Έ≤-27 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/ProjMemAdjoin.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mem_adjoin` / `spinSOpMinus_mem_adjoin` | **Ladder operators live in `Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(Έ±)}}`**: `≈€^+, ≈€^- βàà Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(1)}, ≈€^{(2)}, ≈€^{(3)}}`. Direct consequence of Έ≤-26 (`≈€^¬± = ≈€^{(1)} ¬± i ¬Ζ ≈€^{(2)}`) and the fact that subalgebras are closed under `β³²`-linear combinations (Έ≤-28 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMMemAdjoin.lean` |
| `single_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Immediate-neighbor matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(Έ±)}}`**: `E_{i, i+1}, E_{i+1, i} βàà Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(1)}, ≈€^{(2)}, ≈€^{(3)}}`. Combines Έ≤-10 (`≈€^+ ¬Ζ P_{i+1} = βàö((i+1)(N-i)) ¬Ζ E_{i, i+1}`) with Έ≤-27 (`P_k βàà adjoin`) and Έ≤-28 (`≈€^¬± βàà adjoin`); the ladder coefficient is non-zero on the valid range and the subalgebra is closed under multiplication and scalar `smul`. Step toward expressing every matrix unit as a polynomial in `{≈€^{(Έ±)}}` (Έ≤-29 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/NeighborUnitAdjoin.lean` |
| `single_offset_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_offset_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Arbitrary stride-(k+1) matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(Έ±)}}`**: `E_{i, i+(k+1)}, E_{i+(k+1), i} βàà Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(Έ±)}}` for any `k`. Induction on `k`: base case is Έ≤-29; inductive step chains via `Matrix.single_mul_single_same` (`E_{i,j} ¬Ζ E_{j,k} = E_{i,k}`) (Έ≤-30 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/OffsetUnitAdjoin.lean` |
| `matrix_single_mem_adjoin` | **Every matrix unit `E_{i,j}` lives in `Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(Έ±)}}`**. Three-case split: `i = j` reduces to Έ≤-27 via `Matrix.diagonal_single` (`E_{i,i} = P_i`); `i.val < j.val` is Έ≤-30 upper; `j.val < i.val` is Έ≤-30 lower. Last building block before the spanning theorem (Έ≤-31 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AllUnitsAdjoin.lean` |
| `matrix_mem_adjoin` / **`spinS_adjoin_eq_top`** | **πüé· Tasaki ¬ß2.1 Problem 2.1.a (P1d''') general-`S`**: every operator on the `(2S+1)`-dimensional spin-`S` Hilbert space `β³²^{N+1}` is a polynomial in `{1Χ², ≈€^{(1)}, ≈€^{(2)}, ≈€^{(3)}}`. Equivalently, `Algebra.adjoin β³² {≈€^{(1)}, ≈€^{(2)}, ≈€^{(3)}} = βäΛ`. Proof: every matrix unit `E_{i,j} βàà adjoin` (Έ≤-31), so by the entry-wise decomposition `M = βàë_{i,j} M_{i,j} βÄΔ E_{i,j}` (`Matrix.matrix_eq_sum_single`) and the linearity of the subalgebra, every matrix is in the adjoin (Έ≤-32 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/SpanningTheorem.lean` |
| `ManyBodyOpS` / `onSiteS` / `spinSSiteOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}` | **Multi-site spin-`S` operator space** indexed by configurations `œÉ : Έ¦ βÜ£ Fin (N + 1)`, with the site-embedded operator `onSiteS i A` acting as `A` on site `i` and as the identity elsewhere; site-specialised `≈€_i^{(Έ±)}, ≈€_i^¬±`. Hermiticity preservation `onSiteS_isHermitian` lifts from single-site to multi-site (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Phase B-Έ≤ Έ≤-3a, Issue #412) | `Quantum/SpinS/MultiSite.lean` |

| `pauliX_eq_indicator` / `onSite_pauliX_mulVec_apply` | closed-form `pauliX a b = if b = 1 - a then 1 else 0`, lifted to `((onSite x œÉ^x).mulVec v) œ³ = v (siteFlipAt œ³ x)` for any state `v` (general extension of the basis-state action) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSign_prod_siteFlipAt` | `βàè_y ΈΒ((siteFlipAt œ³ x) y) = -(βàè_y ΈΒ(œ³ y))` βÄî the per-site flip swaps `ΈΒ(œ³ x)` with `ΈΒ(1 - œ³ x) = -ΈΒ(œ³ x)`, flipping the total sign | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_pauliX_mulVec` | multi-site sign-flip equivariance for `œÉ^x` (Tasaki ¬ß2.3 (2.3.14) at Έ± = 1): `Έ‰Χ²_tot ((onSite x œÉ^x) v) = (-(onSite x œÉ^x))(Έ‰Χ²_tot v)` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_pauliY_mulVec` | multi-site sign-flip equivariance for `œÉ^y` (Tasaki ¬ß2.3 (2.3.14) at Έ± = 2): `Έ‰Χ²_tot ((onSite x œÉ^y) v) = (-(onSite x œÉ^y))(Έ‰Χ²_tot v)`. The proof handles the per-site `¬±i` factor via `conj(pauliY_sign(1 - s)) = pauliY_sign(s)` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_add` / `_smul` / `_real_smul` | multi-spin `Έ‰Χ²_tot` is additive, antilinear in the scalar (`Έ‰Χ²_tot(c βÄΔ v) = conj(c) βÄΔ Έ‰Χ²_tot v`), and real-linear (special case of antilinearity at real `r`) βÄî foundational for lifting Pauli-axis equivariance to bilinear / Heisenberg-type Hamiltonian forms | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_spinHalfOp{1,2,3}_mulVec` | Tasaki ¬ß2.3 (2.3.14) for spin-1/2 ops `≈€^(Έ±) = œÉ^(Έ±) / 2`: `Έ‰Χ²_tot ((onSite x ≈€^(Έ±)) v) = (-(onSite x ≈€^(Έ±)))(Έ‰Χ²_tot v)` for Έ± = 1, 2, 3 βÄî direct corollaries of the Pauli versions by scalar (1/2) multiplication | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_spinHalfDot_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the bilinear `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y`** (Tasaki ¬ß2.3): `Έ‰Χ²_tot ((≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y) v) = (≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y)(Έ‰Χ²_tot v)` βÄî two equivariance `-1` factors cancel; sums per-axis | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the Heisenberg Hamiltonian** (Tasaki ¬ß2.3): for real coupling `J` (`conj(J(x,y)) = J(x,y)`), `Έ‰Χ²_tot ((H J) v) = (H J)(Έ‰Χ²_tot v)`. Combines per-bond invariance + Έ‰Χ²_tot antilinearity (J reality) + additivity (over double-sum) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `openChainCoupling_conj` / `periodicChainCoupling_conj` | every entry of `openChainCoupling N J` (resp. `periodicChainCoupling N J`) is real (under complex conjugation), since `J : β³ù` makes `(-(J : β³²))` real-valued | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_openChainHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_periodicChainHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_squareLatticeHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_squareTorusHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_cubicLatticeHeisenberg_mulVec` | concrete time-reversal invariance: the open / periodic chain, the 2D open square / torus, and the 3D cubic Heisenberg Hamiltonians all commute with `Έ‰Χ²_tot` for any real coupling `J : β³ù`. Backed by `*Coupling_conj` reality lemmas in `HeisenbergChain.lean` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_basisVec_upDown` / `_basisVec_basisSwap_upDown` | `Έ‰Χ²_tot |βÜëβÜ™βü© = -|βÜ™βÜëβü©` and `Έ‰Χ²_tot |βÜ™βÜëβü© = -|βÜëβÜ™βü©` on `Fin 2` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_singlet` | the two-site spin singlet `|βÜëβÜ™βü© - |βÜ™βÜëβü©` is **time-reversal invariant** (Tasaki ¬ß2.3 / ¬ßA.3): being the SU(2) `S = 0` representation, it survives `Έ‰Χ²_tot` unchanged | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_triplet_zero` | the triplet `m = 0` state `|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©` is **anti-invariant** under `Έ‰Χ²_tot`: `Έ‰Χ²_tot (|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©) = -(|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©)` (the symmetric combination picks up a minus sign from the per-basis-vector flip) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |

### Multi-body operator space (abstract lattice)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß2.2, pp. 21-26 (tensor-product Hilbert space and site-local
operators). The lattice `Έ¦` is an arbitrary finite set with decidable
equality; specializing to `Έ¦ = Fin N` recovers an `N`-site chain.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `ManyBodyOp Έ¦` | `Matrix (Έ¦ βÜ£ Fin 2) (Έ¦ βÜ£ Fin 2) β³²` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite i A` | site-embedded operator at `i : Έ¦` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_isHermitian` | `A.IsHermitian βÜ£ (onSite i A).IsHermitian` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_add`, `onSite_sub`, `onSite_zero`, `onSite_smul`, `onSite_one` | linearity of the site embedding and `onSite i 1 = 1` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_of_ne` | distinct-site commutation (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x βâ† y`, S = 1/2) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `basisVec` / `onSite_mulVec_basisVec` | tensor-product basis states and their action under site operators (Tasaki (2.2.1)/(2.2.4)) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_same` | same-site product `onSite i A ¬Ζ onSite i B = onSite i (A ¬Ζ B)` (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x = y`) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_same` | same-site commutator `[onSite i A, onSite i B] = onSite i [A, B]` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `Matrix.IsHermitian.mul_of_commute` | commuting Hermitians multiply Hermitian | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |

### Total spin operator (Tasaki ¬ß2.2 eq. (2.2.7), (2.2.8))

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body

### Two-site spin inner product (Tasaki ¬ß2.2 eq. (2.2.16))

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß2.2 eq. (2.2.16), p. 24.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfDot x y` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y := ΈΘ_{Έ±} onSite x ≈€^(Έ±) ¬Ζ onSite y ≈€^(Έ±)` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_eq_plus_minus` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y = (1/2)(≈€_x^+ ≈€_y^- + ≈€_x^- ≈€_y^+) + ≈€_x^(3) ≈€_y^(3)` (Tasaki (2.2.16)) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_comm` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y = ≈€_y ¬Ζ ≈€_x` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_self` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_x = (3/4) ¬Ζ 1` (the S(S+1) = 3/4 identity for S = 1/2) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_isHermitian` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y` is Hermitian | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_eq_sum_dot` | `(≈€_tot)¬≤ = ΈΘ_{x,y} ≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfPairSpinSq` / `spinHalfPairSpinSq_eq` | `(≈€_x + ≈€_y)¬≤ = 2¬Ζ(≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y) + ≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_x + ≈€_y ¬Ζ ≈€_y` (Tasaki (2.2.18)) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}` | `[≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y, ≈€_tot^(Έ±)] = 0` for Έ± βàà {1, 2, 3} (SU(2) invariance, Tasaki (2.2.17)) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_commutator_totalSpinHalfOpPlus/Minus` | `[≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y, ≈€^¬±_tot] = 0` (ladder-operator version of SU(2) invariance) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_parallel` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y |œÉβü© = (1/4) |œÉβü©` when `œÉ x = œÉ y` and `x βâ† y` (Tasaki (2.2.19) parallel case) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_both_up/down` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y |βÜëβÜëβü© = (1/4) |βÜëβÜëβü©`, `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y |βÜ™βÜ™βü© = (1/4) |βÜ™βÜ™βü©` (Tasaki (2.2.19) triplet `m = ¬±1`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `basisSwap` / `basisSwap_involutive` / `basisSwap_antiparallel` | site-swap of `œÉ` at `x, y`, involutive and preserves anti-parallelism | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_antiparallel` | `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y |œÉβü© = (1/2) |swap œÉβü© - (1/4) |œÉβü©` when `œÉ x βâ† œÉ y` (anti-parallel case) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_singlet` | singlet eigenvalue `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y (|œÉβü© - |swap œÉβü©) = -(3/4) (|œÉβü© - |swap œÉβü©)` (Tasaki (2.2.19) singlet `S = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_triplet_anti` | triplet `m = 0` eigenvalue `≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y (|œÉβü© + |swap œÉβü©) = (1/4) (|œÉβü© + |swap œÉβü©)` (Tasaki (2.2.19) triplet `m = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian` | `H = ΈΘ_{x,y} J(x,y) ≈€_x ¬Ζ ≈€_y` (general Heisenberg-type Hamiltonian) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}` | `[H, ≈€_tot^(Έ±)] = 0` for all axes (Tasaki (2.2.13) SU(2) invariance) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{Plus,Minus}` | `[H, ≈€^¬±_tot] = 0` (ladder form of SU(2) invariance) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfSquared` | `Commute H ≈€tot¬≤` βÄî the Casimir operator-level form of SU(2) invariance (consequence of `[H, ≈€tot^Έ±] = 0` for each Έ±, via `Commute.mul_right` and `.add_right`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_preserves_totalSpinHalfSquared_eigenvalue` | if `≈€tot¬≤ ¬Ζ v = S ¬Ζ v` then `≈€tot¬≤ ¬Ζ (H ¬Ζ v) = S ¬Ζ (H ¬Ζ v)` βÄî operator-level simultaneous diagonalisation of `H` and the SU(2) Casimir | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfOpPlus_mul_pauliZ` / `pauliZ_mul_spinHalfOpPlus` | `œÉ^+ ¬Ζ œÉ^z = -œÉ^+` and `œÉ^z ¬Ζ œÉ^+ = œÉ^+` βÄî the (anti)commutation at the single-site Pauli algebra level, used for the Jordan-Wigner cross-site CAR | `Quantum/SpinHalfBasis.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_basisVec_const` | `≈€_tot¬≤ |s s βÄΠ sβü© = (N(N+2)/4) |s s βÄΠ sβü©` for any constant `s : Fin 2` (Casimir eigenvalue at maximum total spin `S = N/2`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_basisVec_all_up/down` | specializations of the above to `s = 0` (all-up) and `s = 1` (all-down) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOp{Minus,Plus}_pow_basisVec_const` | for any `s : Fin 2` and `k : β³ï`, `≈€tot¬≤ ¬Ζ (≈€tot^βà™)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü© = (|Έ¦|¬Ζ(|Έ¦|+2)/4) ¬Ζ (≈€tot^βà™)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©` βÄî the iterated ladder iterates remain in the maximum-total-spin SU(2) representation `S = Smax = |Έ¦|/2` (Casimir invariance, Tasaki ¬ß2.4) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_const` | `H |sβÄΠsβü© = (ΈΘ_{x,y} J(x,y)¬Ζ(if x=y then 3/4 else 1/4)) ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©` βÄî every Heisenberg-type Hamiltonian acts on a uniformly-aligned basis state as a scalar; bilinear-sum lift of Tasaki ¬ß2.4 eq. (2.4.5), p. 32 (`-≈€_x¬Ζ≈€_y |ΈΠβÜëβü© = -S¬≤ |ΈΠβÜëβü©` for `S = 1/2`, `x βâ† y`), with the diagonal `S(S+1) = 3/4` contribution recorded explicitly | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_all_up/down` | specialisations of the above to `s = 0` (all-up) / `s = 1` (all-down) βÄî the eigenvector property of the fully-polarised states; ground-state status (Tasaki's `E_GS = -|B|¬ΖS¬≤`) requires extra ferromagnetic structure on `J` and is not asserted here | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_basisVec_const` | `H ¬Ζ (≈€_tot^+ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©) = c_J ¬Ζ (≈€_tot^+ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©)` βÄî `≈€_tot^+` preserves the H-eigenvalue on a constant-spin basis state (corollary of SU(2) invariance, Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_basisVec_const` | same with `≈€_tot^-` βÄî the canonical lowering ladder Tasaki uses to enumerate the ferromagnetic ground states `|ΈΠ_Mβü©` (eq. (2.4.9), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_pow_basisVec_const` | iterated form: for any constant `s : Fin 2` and any `k : β³ï`, `H ¬Ζ ((≈€_tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©) = c_J ¬Ζ ((≈€_tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©)`; specialised at `s = 0` this gives the unnormalised Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.9), p. 33 βÄî every iterate `(≈€_tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |ΈΠβÜëβü©` lies in the same H-eigenspace as `|ΈΠβÜëβü©` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_pow_basisVec_const` | companion iterated form for `≈€_tot^+`: for any constant `s : Fin 2` and any `k : β³ï`, `H ¬Ζ ((≈€_tot^+)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©) = c_J ¬Ζ ((≈€_tot^+)^k ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©)` (corollary of SU(2) invariance, Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.7), iterated) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}` | for any `J` and `ΈΗ : β³ù`, `H` commutes with the global rotation `Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ = exp(-iΈΗ ≈€_tot^Έ±)` (composes `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{Έ±}` with `totalSpinHalfRot{Έ±}_commute_of_commute`; the operator-level form of Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}_basisVec_const` | for any `J`, `ΈΗ`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H ¬Ζ (Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©) = c_J ¬Ζ (Ο¦^(Έ±)_ΈΗ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©)` βÄî the rotated (single-axis) constant-spin state shares the H-eigenvalue (Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfRot32_basisVec_const` | for any `J`, `ΈΗ`, `œï`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H ¬Ζ (Ο¦^(3)_œï ¬Ζ Ο¦^(2)_ΈΗ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©) = c_J ¬Ζ (Ο¦^(3)_œï ¬Ζ Ο¦^(2)_ΈΗ ¬Ζ |sβÄΠsβü©)` βÄî the two-step spin-coherent state of Tasaki eq. (2.4.6) (`|Έû_ΈΗ,œïβü©` for `s = 0`) is an H-eigenvector with the same eigenvalue as the constant configuration (Tasaki eq. (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_two_site_singlet` | `≈€_tot¬≤ (|βÜëβÜ™βü© - |βÜ™βÜëβü©) = 0` for `Έ¦ = Fin 2` (singlet, `S = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_two_site_triplet_zero` | `≈€_tot¬≤ (|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©) = 2(|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©)` for `Έ¦ = Fin 2` (triplet `m = 0`, `S = 1`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfOp3_mulVec_two_site_singlet` | the two-site singlet has zero `≈€_tot^(3)` magnetization | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_totalOnSite` | `[onSite x SΈ±, ΈΘ_z onSite z SΈ≤] = onSite x [SΈ±, SΈ≤]` | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |

### One-dimensional open-chain quantum Ising

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß3.3 eq. (3.3.1), p. 55 (transverse-field Ising on an open
chain). Our formalization uses the Pauli convention `œÉ = 2¬ΖS` and an
explicit bond coupling `J`.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h` | `H = -J ΈΘ œÉ^z_i œÉ^z_{i+1} - h ΈΘ œÉ^x_i` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_isHermitian` | `H` is Hermitian for real `J`, `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot x y` | the Ising bond operator `œÉ^z_x ¬Ζ œÉ^z_y` (generic in `Έ¦`) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot_isHermitian` | each bond operator is Hermitian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric (J : Έ¦ βÜ£ Έ¦ βÜ£ β³²) (h : β³²)` | **graph-friendly** Ising Hamiltonian `ΈΘ J(x,y) œÉ^z_x œÉ^z_y βà£ h ΈΘ œÉ^x_x` for any finite `Έ¦` and pairwise coupling `J`; specialises to chain / graph / lattice via the choice of `J` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric_isHermitian` | Hermitian for entry-wise real `J` and real `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph G J h` | graph wrapper: `isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf G J) h`; double-sum convention matches Heisenberg-on-graph | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph_isHermitian` | Hermitian for real `J, h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph G Έ≤ J h` | Gibbs state of the graph-built Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_isHermitian` / `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_commute_hamiltonian` | Hermiticity (real `J, h`) and commute with the Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.sum_pathGraph_forward` / `sum_pathGraph_backward` / `sum_pathGraph_adj` | sum-decomposition helpers for `pathGraph (N+1)` adjacency: `ΈΘ_{x,y}` over ordered adjacent pairs = `ΈΘ_{i:Fin N} (f i.cs i.s + f i.s i.cs)` | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `pathGraphParityColoring` / `pathGraph_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of `pathGraph (N + 1)` (`i βÜΠ i.val % 2`) and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Underpins the NΟ©el state (`Quantum/NeelState.lean`) and the Marshall-Lieb-Mattis theorem (Tasaki ¬ß2.5) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `cycleGraphEvenParityColoring` / `cycleGraph_even_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of the even cycle `cycleGraph (2 * K + 2)` and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Wrap-around case `(2K+1) + 1 βâΓ 0` still flips parity because the cycle length is even (odd cycles are not bipartite) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_eq_isingHamiltonianGeneric` | **generic-N bridge**: `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h = isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf (pathGraph (N+1)) (-J/2)) h`. The proof itself is the robust regression test | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_mul_hamiltonian_im` | for Hermitian `O`, `(βü®H_Ising ¬Ζ Oβü©_Έ≤).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_anticommutator_im` | for Hermitian `A, B`, `(βü®A¬ΖB + B¬ΖAβü©_Έ≤).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_commutator_re` | for Hermitian `A, B`, `(βü®A¬ΖB βà£ B¬ΖAβü©_Έ≤).re = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsHamiltonianVariance_im` | `(Var_Έ≤(H_Ising)).im = 0` (energy variance real) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsing_partitionFn_im` | `(partitionFn Έ≤ H_Ising).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_ofReal_re_eq` | for Hermitian `O`, `((βü®Oβü©_Έ≤).re : β³²) = βü®Oβü©_Έ≤` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsState_pow_trace` | `Tr(œ¹_Έ≤^n) = Z(nΈ≤) / Z(Έ≤)^n` for the Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_self_eq` | `βü®H_Isingβü©_Έ≤ = -J ¬Ζ βàë βü®œÉ^z œÉ^zβü©_Έ≤ + (-h) ¬Ζ βàë βü®œÉ^xβü©_Έ≤` (energy as bond + transverse-field decomposition) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

### Gibbs state (Tasaki ¬ß3.3)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß3.3.

All theorems in this module are fully proved with **zero `sorry`**.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `gibbsExp Έ≤ H` | `exp(-Έ≤H) := Matrix.exp (-Έ≤ βÄΔ H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isHermitian` | `exp(-Έ≤H)` is Hermitian (when `H` is Hermitian) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_zero` | `exp(-0¬ΖH) = 1` (Tasaki ¬ß3.3, pp. 75βÄ™78) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add` | `exp(-(Έ≤β²¹+Έ≤β²²)H) = exp(-Έ≤β²¹H) ¬Ζ exp(-Έ≤β²²H)` (one-parameter group) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add_of_commute_hamiltonians` | `exp(-Έ≤(Hβ²¹+Hβ²²)) = exp(-Έ≤Hβ²¹) ¬Ζ exp(-Έ≤Hβ²²)` for commuting `Hβ²¹, Hβ²²` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_neg_mul_self` | `exp(Έ≤H) ¬Ζ exp(-Έ≤H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_self_mul_neg` | `exp(-Έ≤H) ¬Ζ exp(Έ≤H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isUnit` | `exp(-Έ≤H)` is invertible | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_ne_zero` | `exp(-Έ≤H) βâ† 0` (corollary of `gibbsExp_isUnit`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_ne_zero` | `œ¹_Έ≤ βâ† 0` when `Z(Έ≤) βâ† 0` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_inv` | `(œ¹_Έ≤)β¹Μ¬Ι = Z(Έ≤) ¬Ζ e^{Έ≤H}` when `Z(Έ≤) βâ† 0` (general matrix inverse, generalises `gibbsState_zero_inv`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_smul_gibbsState_eq_gibbsExp` | `Z(Έ≤) ¬Ζ œ¹_Έ≤ = e^{-Έ≤H}` when `Z(Έ≤) βâ† 0` (canonical rescaled identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_mul_gibbsExpectation_eq` | `Z(Έ≤) ¬Ζ βü®Aβü©_Έ≤ = Tr(e^{-Έ≤H} ¬Ζ A)` when `Z(Έ≤) βâ† 0` (canonical unnormalised expectation) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_natCast_mul` | `exp(-(n¬ΖΈ≤)H) = (exp(-Έ≤H))^n` for `n : β³ï` (exact discrete semigroup identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_two_mul` | `exp(-(2Έ≤)H) = exp(-Έ≤H) ¬Ζ exp(-Έ≤H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_inv` | `(exp(-Έ≤H))β¹Μ¬Ι = exp(Έ≤H)` (matrix inverse made explicit) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_intCast_mul` | `exp(-(n¬ΖΈ≤)H) = (exp(-Έ≤H))^n` for `n : β³Λ` (integer-power extension) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn Έ≤ H` | `Z := Matrix.trace (exp(-Έ≤H))` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_zero` | `Z(0) = Fintype.card (Έ¦ βÜ£ Fin 2)` (dimension of the Hilbert space) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_zero_ne_zero` | `Z(0) βâ† 0` (concrete sorry-free proof that the partition function is nonzero at Έ≤ = 0) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `Matrix.IsHermitian.trace_im` | for any Hermitian `A : Matrix n n β³²`, `A.trace.im = 0` (generic helper) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_im_of_isHermitian` | for Hermitian `H`, `(partitionFn Έ≤ H).im = 0` (Z is real) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_mul_self_trace` | `Tr(œ¹_Έ≤¬≤) = Z(2Έ≤) / Z(Έ≤)¬≤` (purity / RΟ©nyi-2 entropy precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_pow_trace` | `Tr(œ¹_Έ≤^n) = Z(nΈ≤) / Z(Έ≤)^n` for any `n : β³ï` (RΟ©nyi-n entropy precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_zero` | `œ¹_0 = (1/dim) ¬Ζ I` (maximally mixed state at infinite temperature) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_zero_inv` | `œ¹_0β¹Μ¬Ι = dim ¬Ζ I` (matrix inverse at Έ≤ = 0) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_zero` | `βü®Aβü©_0 = (1/dim) ¬Ζ Tr A` (high-temperature limit) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState Έ≤ H` | `œ¹ := (1/Z) βÄΔ exp(-Έ≤H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_trace` | `Tr(œ¹) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_isHermitian` | `œ¹` is Hermitian | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation Έ≤ H O` | `βü®Oβü© := Matrix.trace (œ¹ * O)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_one` | `βü®1βü© = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_add` | `βü®Oβ²¹ + Oβ²²βü© = βü®Oβ²¹βü© + βü®Oβ²²βü©` (linearity in observable) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_smul` | `βü®c ¬Ζ Oβü© = c ¬Ζ βü®Oβü©` (scalar linearity, `c : β³²`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_neg` | `βü®-Oβü© = -βü®Oβü©` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sub` | `βü®A - Bβü© = βü®Aβü© - βü®Bβü©` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sum` | `βü®βàë i βàà s, f iβü© = βàë i βàà s, βü®f iβü©` (finite-sum linearity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

### Heisenberg chain (Tasaki ¬ß3.5)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ¬ß3.5, p. 89.

| Lean name | Statement | File |

| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.couplingOf G J` | the canonical pairwise coupling `Έ¦ βÜ£ Έ¦ βÜ£ β³²` of a `SimpleGraph G` with uniform edge weight `J`: returns `J` on edges of `G`, zero otherwise (graph-centric bridge) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.couplingOf_symm` / `_self` / `_real` | symmetry (from `G.Adj` symmetry), vanishing on the diagonal (from irreflexivity), and reality (for real edge weight) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |

| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_eq` | for `N = 1` (the 2-site open chain on `Fin 2`), `H_open = -2J ¬Ζ spinHalfDot 0 1` (explicit one-bond reduction; Tasaki ¬ß2.4 simplest concrete instance) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_mulVec_basisVec_all_up` | `H_open(N=1) ¬Ζ |βÜëβÜëβü© = -(J/2) ¬Ζ |βÜëβÜëβü©` βÄî `|βÜëβÜëβü©` lies in the `S = 1` triplet sector and is an exact eigenvector with eigenvalue `-J/2` (this is the ferromagnetic ground state for `J < 0`) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_mulVec_basisVec_singlet` | `H_open(N=1) ¬Ζ (|βÜëβÜ™βü© - |βÜ™βÜëβü©) = (3J/2) ¬Ζ (|βÜëβÜ™βü© - |βÜ™βÜëβü©)` βÄî singlet eigenvalue, the antiferromagnetic ground state for `J > 0` (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 concrete instance) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_mulVec_basisVec_all_down` | `H_open(N=1) ¬Ζ |βÜ™βÜ™βü© = -(J/2) ¬Ζ |βÜ™βÜ™βü©` βÄî all-down state has the same eigenvalue as all-up (both are `S = 1` triplet states) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_mulVec_basisVec_triplet_zero` | `H_open(N=1) ¬Ζ (|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©) = -(J/2) ¬Ζ (|βÜëβÜ™βü© + |βÜ™βÜëβü©)` βÄî triplet `m = 0` state, completing the 3-fold degenerate triplet representation `S = 1` with eigenvalue `-J/2` | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_three_site_eq` | for `N = 2` (the 3-site open chain on `Fin 3`, 2 bonds), `H_open = -2J ¬Ζ (spinHalfDot 0 1 + spinHalfDot 1 2)` βÄî explicit two-bond reduction | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_three_site_mulVec_basisVec_all_up` | `H_open(N=2) ¬Ζ |βÜëβÜëβÜëβü© = -J ¬Ζ |βÜëβÜëβÜëβü©` βÄî confirming the linear scaling `E(|βÜë..βÜëβü©) = -N¬ΖJ/2` (here `N = 2` bonds, `J = 1` per bond) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainCoupling_sum_eq` | for any `N : β³ï`, `ΈΘ_{x,y βàà Fin (N+1)} openChainCoupling N J x y = -(2N ¬Ζ J : β³²)` (the bond-counting lemma: each of the `N` unordered nearest-neighbour bonds is counted in both orientations) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_const` | for any `N : β³ï`, `J : β³ù`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H_open ¬Ζ |s..sβü© = -(N¬ΖJ/2 : β³²) ¬Ζ |s..sβü©` βÄî both `s = 0` (all-up) and `s = 1` (all-down) share the same eigenvalue by SU(2) symmetry | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_all_up` | `s = 0` specialisation of the above (Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.5)/(2.4.1) ferromagnetic ground-state energy `E_GS = -|B|¬ΖS¬≤` for `S = 1/2`, `|B| = N` bonds) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_all_down` | `s = 1` specialisation: same eigenvalue `-(N¬ΖJ/2)` for the all-down state by SU(2) symmetry | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_pow_basisVec_all_up` | for any `N : β³ï`, `J : β³ù`, `k : β³ï`, `H_open ¬Ζ ((≈€tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |βÜë..βÜëβü©) = -(N¬ΖJ/2 : β³²) ¬Ζ ((≈€tot^-)^k ¬Ζ |βÜë..βÜëβü©)` βÄî the unnormalised Tasaki ¬ß2.4 (2.4.9) ferromagnetic ground states `|ΈΠ_Mβü©` made explicit on the chain (combines PRs #82 + #98) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_pow_basisVec_all_down` | dual ladder from `|βÜ™..βÜ™βü©`, same eigenvalue `-(N¬ΖJ/2)` | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | `H_open` preserves every magnetisation subspace `H_M` (chain specialisation of PR #91) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `periodicChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | `H_periodic` preserves every magnetisation subspace `H_M` (chain specialisation of PR #91) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |

### Perron-Frobenius theorem (`Math/PerronFrobenius.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean`, `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean`)

Perron-Frobenius theorem for nonneg irreducible/primitive matrices (Issue #405, closed).
The sorry in `exists_pos_eigenvec_max` is eliminated via the Collatz-Wielandt port (PRs AβÄ™C).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `Matrix.IsPrimitive.of_irreducible_pos_diagonal` | irreducible nonneg + positive diagonal βÜ£ primitive (Seneta ¬ß1.1, Prop. 1.3, p. 17) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.collatzWielandtFn` | CW function `min_{i\|x_i>0} (Ax)_i/x_i` (Seneta ¬ß1.2, p. 27) | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.le_any_ratio` | `CW(x) βâΛ (Ax)_i/x_i` for `x_i > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.le_mulVec` | fundamental inequality `CW(x)¬Ζx βâΛ Ax` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.smul_eq` | scale invariance `CW(cx) = CW(x)` for `c > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.upperSemicontinuousOn` | CW is upper-semicontinuous on stdSimplex | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.exists_maximizer` | CW attains its max on stdSimplex (EVT for USC, Seneta ¬ß1.2, p. 28) | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.eq_eigenvalue` | `CW(v) = r` when `Av = r¬Ζv`, `v > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.lt_of_all_ratios_gt` | all ratios `> c` βüΙ `CW(x) > c` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.pos_of_nonneg_eigenvec` | irreducible nonneg + `Av = ΈΦv`, `v βâΞ 0`, `v βâ† 0` βüΙ `v > 0` (standard propagation argument) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.exists_positive_eigenvector_of_primitive` | primitive nonneg βüΙ βàÉ `r > 0`, `v > 0` with `Av = rv` (Seneta ¬ß1.2, pp. 27βÄ™28) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.exists_positive_eigenvector_of_irreducible` | irreducible nonneg βüΙ βàÉ `r > 0`, `v > 0` with `Av = rv` (Seneta ¬ß1.2, pp. 27βÄ™28) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `exists_nonneg_eigenvec_max` | (**sorry**, retained for docs) symmetric nonneg max eigenvalue has nonneg eigenvector | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |
| `exists_pos_eigenvec_max` | (**sorry-free**) irreducible nonneg Hermitian βüΙ max eigenvalue has strictly positive eigenvector | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique` | strictly positive eigenvector unique up to positive scalar | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |

References: E. Seneta, *Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006, ¬ß1.2 (pp. 27βÄ™28);
or4nge19/MCMC: `MCMC/PF/LinearAlgebra/Matrix/PerronFrobenius/`.

### Spin-`S` MarshallβÄ™LiebβÄ™Mattis on the magnetization sector (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 generic S, sector form)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 applied to the
**magnetization-`M` sector** of the un-dressed antiferromagnetic
Heisenberg Hamiltonian on a bipartite graph. The sector subtype
`magConfigS V N M := { œÉ : V βÜ£ Fin (N + 1) // magSumS œÉ = M }` is the
natural index type since the dressed Heisenberg matrix is irreducible
on each sector. The core sector-matrix API lives in
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSector.lean`; the trailing
eigenvalue-uniqueness + complex-form MLM Theorem 2.2 statements
were moved to the companion
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSectorEigenvalueUnique.lean` in
refactor #30 (PR #2829). Tracked in Issue #412.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `magConfigS V N M` | sector subtype of magnetization-`M` configurations (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `RaiseLowerStepSMagSector G œÉ œ³` / `RaiseLowerReachableSMagSector G` | bipartite raise/lower step lifted to `magConfigS` and its reflexive transitive closure (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `raiseLowerReachableSMagSector_bipartiteCompleteGraph` | any two configurations in the same sector are reachable via raise/lower steps under the bipartite-intermediate hypothesis (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Property (iii) generic-S form) |
| `shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N c M` | shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `c¬Ζ1 - dressed_re` restricted to the sector via `Matrix.submatrix Subtype.val Subtype.val`, the input to PF irreducibility |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N M` | dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg COMPLEX matrix restricted to the sector |
| `isIrreducible_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | `Matrix.IsIrreducible` for the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Έ≥-3 final, MLM PF input) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector existence for the shifted sector matrix (`r > 0`, `v > 0` componentwise) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector uniqueness on the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 nondegeneracy) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF on the dressed sector matrix at eigenvalue `c - r` (Tasaki ¬ß2.5 dressed-form ground state) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #856) |
| `pos_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector positive eigenvectors share the same eigenvalue (Rayleigh identity for symmetric matrices, PR #856) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_heisenberg` / `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_dressed` | matrix relations `dressed = sign¬Ζsign¬Ζheis` and inverse via `sign¬≤ = 1` (PR #853) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_dressed_eigenvec` | Marshall sign conjugation of dressed sector eigenvector to un-dressed Heisenberg sector eigenvector (PR #853) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_heis_eigenvec` | inverse Marshall conjugation (PR #854) |
| `exists_marshallSign_eigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector ground-state existence with Marshall sign structure (PR #853) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #854) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvalue uniqueness (PR #856) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState` | bundled Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 (existence + same-eigenvalue uniqueness, PR #855) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2: existence + forced eigenvalue uniqueness + eigenvector uniqueness (PR #859) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_isHermitian` | complex sector matrix is Hermitian for real coupling (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_apply_eq_ofReal` | for real coupling, complex sector entries equal real-form entries embedded in `β³²` (PR #857) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_ofReal` | real βÜ£ complex eigenvector lift (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_re_of_complex_eigenvec` | complex βÜ£ real real-part extraction (PR #861) |
| `exists_marshallSign_complexEigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 ground-state existence on the un-dressed quantum Heisenberg sector matrix (PR #860) |
| `marshallPositive_complexEigenvec_re_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Marshall-positive uniqueness via real-part extraction (PR #862) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 on the complex sector matrix (PR #863) |

The complex-form `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full`
is the COMPLEX-Hilbert-space form of Tasaki ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 in the
magnetization sector: the ground state of the un-dressed quantum
Heisenberg Hamiltonian restricted to the sector is unique (up to a
positive real scalar in its real part) and has the Marshall sign
structure `ΈΠ œÉ := ((sign A œÉ.1).re * v œÉ : β³²)` with `v > 0`.

References: H. Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, Springer 2020, ¬ß2.5 Theorem 2.2 (pp. 39βÄ™43); E. Seneta,
*Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006,
¬ß1.2 (pp. 27βÄ™28) for the underlying PerronβÄ™Frobenius theorem.

### Spin-`S` saturated ferromagnetic state (Tasaki ¬ß2.4 generalised)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki ¬ß2.4 P1i for the
**saturated ferromagnet**: the all-aligned (constant-spin) basis
state `|œÉ_βäΛβü© = βä½_x |cβü©` with `œÉ x = c` for all `x : V`. The two
extremal weights `c = 0` (highest weight, "all up") and
`c = Fin.last N` (lowest weight, "all down") are the highest- and
lowest-weight vectors of the `J_tot = |V|¬ΖS = |V|¬ΖN/2` irreducible
SU(2) representation in the multi-site Hilbert space. Tracked in
Issue #412; assembled in PRs #875βÄ™#879. All theorems live in
`Quantum/SpinS/AllAlignedState.lean`.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `allAlignedConfigS V N c` | constant configuration `œÉ x = c` (PR #875) |
| `allAlignedStateS V N c` | basis state at constant `c`, equal to `basisVecS (allAlignedConfigS V N c)` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magSumS = |V|¬Ζc.val` (PR #875) |
| `magEigenvalueS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magEigenvalueS = |V|¬ΖN/2 βà£ |V|¬Ζc` (PR #875) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_allAlignedStateS` | `≈€^z_tot ¬Ζ |cβü© = (|V|¬ΖN/2 βà£ |V|¬Ζc) ¬Ζ |cβü©` for any `c` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | `c = 0` βüΙ `magSumS = 0` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_pos_of_ne_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | the all-up configuration is the **unique** `magSumS = 0` configuration (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS_last` | `c = Fin.last N` βüΙ `magSumS = |V|¬ΖN` (PR #876) |
| `magSumS_lt_card_mul_of_ne_allAlignedConfigS_last` | the all-down configuration is the unique configuration with `magSumS = |V|¬ΖN` (PR #876) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | the **all-up state is a Heisenberg eigenvector for ANY coupling** βÄî magnetization conservation `[H, ≈€^z_tot] = 0` + uniqueness of the M=0 configuration (PR #875) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero_eigenvalue` | explicit Heisenberg eigenvalue formula on all-up: `ΈΘ_x J(x,x)¬ΖN(N+2)/4 + ΈΘ_{xβâ†y} J(x,y)¬ΖN¬≤/4` (PR #875) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` / `_eigenvalue` | symmetric c = N (all-down) Heisenberg eigenvector + same eigenvalue formula (PR #876) |
| `onSiteS_spinSOpPlus_apply_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | `(onSiteS x ≈€^+) œÉ' œÉ_βäΛ = 0` (PR #877) |
| `onSiteS_spinSOpPlus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | `(onSiteS x ≈€^+).mulVec |œÉ_βäΛβü© = 0` (PR #877) |
| `totalSpinSOpPlus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | **`≈€^+_tot ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΛβü© = 0`** (highest-weight annihilation, PR #877) |
| `onSiteS_spinSOpMinus_apply_allAlignedConfigS_last` / `_mulVec_` / `totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric lowest-weight annihilation `≈€^-_tot ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΞβü© = 0` (PR #877) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | the all-up state is a `(≈€_tot)¬≤`-eigenvector (PR #878) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_apply_diag_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | explicit Casimir diagonal value `|V|¬ΖN(N+2)/4 + (|V|¬≤βà£|V|)¬ΖN¬≤/4` (PR #878) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero_eigenvalue` | **`(≈€_tot)¬≤ ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΛβü© = (|V|¬ΖN/2)¬Ζ(|V|¬ΖN/2 + 1) ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΛβü©`** βÄî operator-level form of "all-up is the highest-weight vector of the J_tot = |V|¬ΖS irreducible SU(2) representation" (PR #878) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` / `_apply_diag_` / `_eigenvalue` | symmetric lowest-weight Casimir eigenvalue (same value) (PR #879) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_commute_totalSpinSOp1` / `_Op2` / `_OpPlus` / `_OpMinus` | `Commute`-form conversions: H commutes with each axis-total operator (PR #881) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_commute_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow` / `_Plus_pow` | iterated power Commute by induction (PR #881) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_allAlignedStateS_zero` | for any k, `(≈€^-_tot)^k ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΛβü©` is a Heisenberg eigenvector at the same eigenvalue as `|œÉ_βäΛβü©` (PR #881) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric for `≈€^+_tot` on all-down (PR #881) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_commute_totalSpinSOp1` / `_Op2` / `_OpPlus` / `_OpMinus` / `_OpMinus_pow` / `_OpPlus_pow` | Casimir Commute-form analogues (PR #882) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_allAlignedStateS_zero` | for any k, `(≈€^-_tot)^k ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΛβü©` preserves the Casimir eigenvalue `(|V|¬ΖN/2)¬Ζ(|V|¬ΖN/2+1)` (PR #882) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric (PR #882) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_commutator_totalSpinSOpMinus` | multi-site Cartan: `[≈€^z_tot, ≈€^-_tot] = -≈€^-_tot` (PR #883) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_commutator_totalSpinSOpPlus` | multi-site Cartan: `[≈€^z_tot, ≈€^+_tot] = +≈€^+_tot` (PR #883) |

| `totalSpinSOp1_eq_one_half_smul_plus_add_minus` / `totalSpinSOp2_eq_one_over_two_I_smul_plus_sub_minus` / `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_totalSpinSOp{1,2,3}_invariant` | **Full Cartesian SU(2) closure of the saturated joint eigenspace**: total-operator identities `≈€^(1)_tot = (1/2)βÄΔ(≈€^+_tot + ≈€^-_tot)` and `≈€^(2)_tot = (1/(2I))βÄΔ(≈€^+_tot βà£ ≈€^-_tot)` (lifted from the single-site definitions of `spinSOp1` / `spinSOp2` via `onSiteS_smul` + `onSiteS_add/sub`); `≈€^(1)_tot` and `≈€^(2)_tot` invariance reduce via these decompositions to the ladder invariances of PRs #2770 / #2771; `≈€^(3)_tot` invariance follows directly from `ladderIterateUp_mem_eigenspace` (each ladder iterate is an `≈€^z_tot`-eigenvector at eigenvalue `m_max βà£ k`, so its `≈€^z_tot`-image is a scalar multiple still in `span(ladderIterateUp) = joint J N`). | `magSubspaceS_eq_bot_of_not_in_spectrum` / `magEigenvalueS_ne_neg_mMax_sub_one` / `totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_succ_card_mul_N_allAlignedStateS_zero` | for `M : β³²` not in the spectrum of `≈€^z_tot`, `magSubspaceS V N M = βäΞ`; `βà£m_max βà£ 1` is outside the spectrum; **boundary annihilation** `(≈€^-_tot)^(|V|¬ΖN + 1) ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΛβü© = 0` (PR #905, file `Quantum/SpinS/LadderBoundaryAnnihilation.lean`). Caps the saturated-ferromagnet ladder at exactly `2m_max + 1` non-zero terms |
| `magEigenvalueS_ne_mMax_add_one` / `totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_succ_card_mul_N_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric raising-side **boundary annihilation** `(≈€^+_tot)^(|V|¬ΖN + 1) ¬Ζ |œÉ_βäΞβü© = 0` via `m_max + 1` off-spectrum (PR #907, extends `LadderBoundaryAnnihilation.lean`) |
| `magEigenvalueS_eq_mMax_iff_allAlignedConfigS_zero` / `magEigenvalueS_eq_neg_mMax_iff_allAlignedConfigS_last` | the extremal eigenvalues `¬±m_max` are achieved by exactly one configuration each (the all-up / all-down constant). ### Single-mode fermion (P2 skeleton)

Phase 2 entry point: the canonical anticommutation algebra of a single
fermion mode acting on `β³²¬≤` with computational basis
`|0βü©` (vacuum) and `|1βü©` (occupied).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `fermionAnnihilation` | `c = !![0, 1; 0, 0] = |0βü©βü®1|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation` | `cβÄ† = !![0, 0; 1, 0] = |1βü©βü®0|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber` | `n = !![0, 0; 0, 1] = |1βü©βü®1|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_eq_creation_mul_annihilation` | `n = cβÄ† ¬Ζ c` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_sq` | `c¬≤ = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation_sq` | `(cβÄ†)¬≤ = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnticomm_self` | `c ¬Ζ cβÄ† + cβÄ† ¬Ζ c = 1` (single-mode CAR) | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_sq` | `n¬≤ = n` (idempotent number operator) | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_conjTranspose` | `cα¥¥ = cβÄ†` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation_conjTranspose` | `(cβÄ†)α¥¥ = c` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |

### Multi-mode fermion via JordanβÄ™Wigner (P2 backbone)

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `jwString N i` | `βàè_{j.val < i.val} œÉ^z_j` (noncomm-product, pairwise commutativity from `onSite_mul_onSite_of_ne`) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `jwString_zero` | `jwString N 0 = 1` (empty product) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiAnnihilation N i` | `c_i = jwString_i ¬Ζ œÉ^+_i` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiCreation N i` | `c_iβÄ† = jwString_i ¬Ζ œÉ^-_i` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiAnnihilation_zero` | `c_0 = œÉ^+_0` (no JW string at the leftmost site) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiCreation_zero` | `c_0βÄ† = œÉ^-_0` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `jwString_commute_onSite` | `Commute (jwString N i) (onSite i A)` (string commutes past same-site operators) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |

| `fermionMultiAnnihilation_anticomm_zero_pos` | **general cross-site CAR `{c_0, c_k} = 0`** for every `k : Fin (N+1)` with `0 < k.val` βÄî generalises the `_zero_one` / `_zero_two_general` specialisations. Proof: reduce to the anticommutator `{œÉ^+_0, jwString N k}`, which vanishes by induction on the string length (base: `{œÉ^+, œÉ^z} = 0` at site 0; step: `œÉ^z_{k-1}` at site `k-1 βâ† 0` commutes past `œÉ^+_0`). | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
